    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

Check. <br>Kick-ass action? Check. <br><br>But a scene from Four's POV? <br><a href="http://www.sodahead.com/living/are-you-afraid-of-needles/question-2257741/?link=ibaf&amp;imgurl=http://www.gifsoup.com/webroot/animatedgifs3/1145666_o.gif&amp;q=faint%20gif" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Well...check! <br><br>This scene (the knife-throwing scene) from Four's POV is perfect fangirling material. I read it, sat absorbed in the moment and then started sniffling at the fact Four wasn't real for a good hour...or two!<br><br>I love the complexity of his character and how real Four is. And sorry, I can't call him Tobias for some reason - it just sounds better as Four! I liked how it shows how his interest in Tris isn't purely "wow-she's-hot/pretty-romantic-wishy-washy", but deeper - how their two souls are so similar, how they are both fighters, survivors and how "looking at her was like waking up". That line was pure magic.<br><br>I LOVE YOU FOUR!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1579928606195968957">Oh man, this was awesome!<br/><br/>But I just wish there was more. Although it was quite lovely seeing things from Four's POV. You know, I've never really swooned over him or found myself connecting to him for some reason. But here I liked him a little more. I particularly enjoyed his observation of the other initiates. I thought that was pretty interesting and informative.<br/><br/>I like that she is not your typical pretty heroine but he finds her determination and solid strength attractive. I can love him a litt</span>
  <span id="freeText1579928606195968957" style="display:none">Oh man, this was awesome!<br /><br />But I just wish there was more. Although it was quite lovely seeing things from Four's POV. You know, I've never really swooned over him or found myself connecting to him for some reason. But here I liked him a little more. I particularly enjoyed his observation of the other initiates. I thought that was pretty interesting and informative.<br /><br />I like that she is not your typical pretty heroine but he finds her determination and solid strength attractive. I can love him a little more for that.<br /><br />And Amar, guys! Doesn't he sound awesome? I really found myself wishing that he was still around. He seemed like a pretty badass and cool leader.<br /><br />You know, I can really see a prequel series/book working well. Imagine reading the times when Eric and Four were initiates. And actually reading about times where the rules weren't as fucked up, where you can see Four more as a teen, rather than the adult he has been forced to grow into due to tough times. And Eric progressing from an asshole to the mentally unstable shit that he is. Sounds interesting, huh. This is a prequel (book or series) that actually makes sense to me.<br /><br />And because I am kind. Here you are :)<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/DivergentSeries?sk=app_276313732461376">https://www.facebook.com/DivergentSer...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14028585285020891581">I just noticed for the first time that there's a comment directly above the review box which asks, "what did you think?"<br/><br/><b>Here's what I thought :</b> Four! Four! Four! Four!<br/><br/>It's a short story. But man...<i>is this a goodie</i>. I hearts teh Four. That's my official stance.<br/><br/>Did I waste 99 cents on a 14 page story? Maybe I did (because really, this should have been a freebie for as short as it is), but his PoV made my night. I didn't realize he had a witty side hiding under all of that seriousness in book 1. I </span>
  <span id="freeText14028585285020891581" style="display:none">I just noticed for the first time that there's a comment directly above the review box which asks, "what did you think?"<br /><br /><b>Here's what I thought :</b> Four! Four! Four! Four!<br /><br />It's a short story. But man...<i>is this a goodie</i>. I hearts teh Four. That's my official stance.<br /><br />Did I waste 99 cents on a 14 page story? Maybe I did (because really, this should have been a freebie for as short as it is), but his PoV made my night. I didn't realize he had a witty side hiding under all of that seriousness in book 1. I wouldn't complain if we got to be in his head more often. This short story covers the knife throwing scene - the one in which Four nicks Tris' ear on purpose. It's not a long enough story to really be a massive spoiler if you haven't read the first book, but it sure isn't going to be as enjoyable to read if you haven't read <i>Divergent</i> because you're being plopped down into a scene which takes place pretty far into the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>She tips her chin up and looks at me with that Abnegation stubbornness I know so well. She may have left them, but they are what's making her strong.<br />I can't tell her that it will be okay, not with Eric here, but I can try to make her strong.<br /><br />~<br /><br />Looking at her is like waking up.<br /><br />~<br /><br />The other factions call us brutish, as if we don't use our minds, but that is all I do here.</blockquote>

<div id="review_674603423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674603423" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674603423?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=continuations-n-retellings">continuations-n-retellings</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674603423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6568490570376610902">one of the best things about having an e-reader are these groovy little splinter-chapters and novellas available digitally that are meant to tide you over until the next book in a series comes out or to re-tell something from another perspective, and it is all fangirl and -boy squee-ish and a really nice thing that authors can do for us.<br/><br/>like this one.<br/><br/>a retelling of a key scene in <i>divergent</i>.<br/><br/>but…here's the thing. while i have loved almost all of the ones mira grant has put out there, and the patri</span>
  <span id="freeText6568490570376610902" style="display:none">one of the best things about having an e-reader are these groovy little splinter-chapters and novellas available digitally that are meant to tide you over until the next book in a series comes out or to re-tell something from another perspective, and it is all fangirl and -boy squee-ish and a really nice thing that authors can do for us.<br><br>like this one.<br><br>a retelling of a key scene in <i>divergent</i>.<br><br>but…here's the thing. while i have loved almost all of the ones mira grant has put out there, and the patrick ness one was great, and the ann aguirre one was fine, sometimes i don't feel they are really necessary. this one falls into that category. it is thirteen pages. thirteen. and while it was only 89 cents, and there's not much that's not worth 89 cents in this world, i just didn't feel satisfied, or that i had read something that really enhanced my enjoyment of <i>divergent</i>. it wasn't particularly <i>illuminating</i>. we get to see what four was thinking. big whoop. we got plenty of his character from the books themselves, and if she had wanted us to know what he was like in these early stages, she'd have written it in the first place, yeah? <br><br>i'm not saying this was a waste of time or anything, and especially considering this is a YA series, and at that age, i would have <i>killed</i> for extra chapters from my favorite books, like how i read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1171087.H__The_Story_of_Heathcliff_s_Journey_Back_to_Wuthering_Heights" title="H. The Story of Heathcliff's Journey Back to Wuthering Heights by Lin Haire-Sargeant" rel="nofollow noopener">H. The Story of Heathcliff's Journey Back to Wuthering Heights</a>, so i get that it makes sense to offer these to readers, and i applaud the gesture, but i feel like this is only that - a gesture. <br><br>gimmie book three, already!!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_318670370" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318670370" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318670370?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=extras">extras</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318670370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer961043759062401086">I love how <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4039811.Veronica_Roth' title='Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Veronica Roth</a> chose this scene for Four's POV. Most authors who have been releasing scenes from the guy's POV lately, always choose a scene where they were making out or something (in which case she probably would have gone with Chapter 31). Like Clare's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13552933.Clockwork_Prince_An_Offering_of_Moonlight__The_Infernal_Devices_Extras___2_1_' title='Clockwork Prince An Offering of Moonlight (The Infernal Devices Extras, #2.1) by Cassandra Clare' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Offering of Moonlight</a>, or Jennifer L. Armentrout's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13323239.Daemon_Extra_from_Obsidian__Lux_' title='Daemon Extra from Obsidian (Lux) by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daemon Extra from Obsidian</a>, which is fun, of course. But this scene of Tobias and Tris is before all that happened. When they were still figuring each other out. It has a range of </span>
  <span id="freeText961043759062401086" style="display:none">I love how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4039811.Veronica_Roth" title="Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Veronica Roth</a> chose this scene for Four's POV. Most authors who have been releasing scenes from the guy's POV lately, always choose a scene where they were making out or something (in which case she probably would have gone with Chapter 31). Like Clare's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13552933.Clockwork_Prince_An_Offering_of_Moonlight__The_Infernal_Devices_Extras___2_1_" title="Clockwork Prince An Offering of Moonlight (The Infernal Devices Extras, #2.1) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">An Offering of Moonlight</a>, or Jennifer L. Armentrout's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13323239.Daemon_Extra_from_Obsidian__Lux_" title="Daemon Extra from Obsidian (Lux) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Daemon Extra from Obsidian</a>, which is fun, of course. But this scene of Tobias and Tris is before all that happened. When they were still figuring each other out. It has a range of emotions instead of just the one, and it reveals much more about his character. Again Roth puts herself above the rest. I love it.</span>

<div id="review_321448525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321448525" />
    <a title="Sarah Ryburn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1054222-sarah-ryburn"><img alt="Sarah Ryburn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1215226427p2/1054222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321448525?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Ryburn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Ryburn" href="/user/show/1054222-sarah-ryburn">Sarah Ryburn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1054222-sarah-ryburn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1054222-sarah-ryburn?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321448525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18314215618715018121">I am rather surprised by the scene choice–in talking with others who've read and loved <i>Divergent</i>, our shared expectation overwhelmingly seemed to be that Roth would pick either "capture the flag/ferris wheel" or "the fear landscape." She mentioned both of these scenes as possibilities she considered. On further reflection, I'm thinking that the fear landscape scene wouldn't have given much insight into the relationship–I think Tobias would have told us alot about himself but very little about hi</span>
  <span id="freeText18314215618715018121" style="display:none">I am rather surprised by the scene choice–in talking with others who've read and loved <i>Divergent</i>, our shared expectation overwhelmingly seemed to be that Roth would pick either "capture the flag/ferris wheel" or "the fear landscape." She mentioned both of these scenes as possibilities she considered. On further reflection, I'm thinking that the fear landscape scene wouldn't have given much insight into the relationship–I think Tobias would have told us alot about himself but very little about his feelings for Tris. Maybe, maybe not. <br /><br />I will admit that I didn't <i>love</i> this scene. It seems to fall short of the quality of her writing in the novel. I am interested in the idea that Four had decided to leave Dauntless and become Factionless. Didn't see that coming, but it fits his character. His character until Tris shows up–once again love turns the world on its ear. My favorite part of the scene, knowing absolutely that Four meant what I thought he meant all along when he snears at Tris that he's fed up waiting for her to figure "it" out. Love me some Four...<br /><br />5.12.12-So. Originally, I gave this three stars, but I've just revisited it after reading and rereading <i>Insurgent</i>, and now I think I really do love it. Five-star <i>love</i> it. This aspect of Roth's writing continually impresses and gratifies-it gets better the more I read it. Each successive reading reveals new depth, and this, I think, requires more than skill with words. She strikes me as such a "thinking" writer. In her blog–post about this scene, she commented that she really spends more time in Tobias's head than she realized and that writing the scene in his voice turned out to be less difficult than she had imagined. This is what I mean. She "spends time" in her characters' heads, and her writing has a quality in consequence that it could not have otherwise. That it could not have if the story relied merely on action and plot sequence. There's plenty of action, to be sure, but character drives the story. Grand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18314215618715018121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2344308556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4961719846104655834"><b>
  <i>“Looking at her is like waking up.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Meh, this wasn't too bad. It's just so damn short and because of that you really don't get much from it. This just gives you some very brief insight into the mind of Four, but otherwise, an unnecessary story. It would have been better as an additional chapter in the back of <i>Divergent</i> or maybe even as a flashback at some point throughout this trilogy. All of this information is already basically known and the difference in character POV didn't change it for </span>
  <span id="freeText4961719846104655834" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Looking at her is like waking up.”</i>
</b><br><br>Meh, this wasn't too bad. It's just so damn short and because of that you really don't get much from it. This just gives you some very brief insight into the mind of Four, but otherwise, an unnecessary story. It would have been better as an additional chapter in the back of <i>Divergent</i> or maybe even as a flashback at some point throughout this trilogy. All of this information is already basically known and the difference in character POV didn't change it for me. I guess it was worth reading this to the extent of getting to see things from his perspective and his motivations. To see his reluctance to do/admit things. I read it because I really like the trilogy and I recommend this to any die-hard <i>Divergent</i> fan. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567297644ra/28081399.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“I feel like someone is pressing me into a mold that does not fit my body, forcing me into the wrong shape.”</i>
</b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356818674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3036728969259726911">oooh Four, how I love you. This short story is awessome! I wish we could have the whole book from his perspective...<br/><br/>I feel like short e-novellas should have their own rating system, because sure they aren't the complete story but they bring something to the table. This story for example brought a LOT to the table when it comes to hundreds of beating hearts who lovingly wait for any mention of Four in Divergent. Free Four is a short re telling of Divergent through Four's eyes, and not just on any</span>
  <span id="freeText3036728969259726911" style="display:none">oooh Four, how I love you. This short story is awessome! I wish we could have the whole book from his perspective...<br /><br />I feel like short e-novellas should have their own rating system, because sure they aren't the complete story but they bring something to the table. This story for example brought a LOT to the table when it comes to hundreds of beating hearts who lovingly wait for any mention of Four in Divergent. Free Four is a short re telling of Divergent through Four's eyes, and not just on any part but the knife throwing scene!! Let's just say it's incredibly nice to be inside Four's head at a time when you didn't know what the hell was going on through those parts. The e-novella is less than 15 pages, sad to say, but it will be a nice fix for those who have just finished Insurgent, or even Divergent, and need a bit more.<br /><br />I give this E-novella a 5/5! Getting to look at some things through Four's eyes is amazing, in fact the only thing I am disappointed about is that we don't get the whole NOVEL through Four's eyes. What do you say guys? Let Veronica Roth take a step into the unthinkable and write Divergent again through Four's eyes?! YES?! Oh please do so, I would so buy that book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3036728969259726911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_478171244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478171244" />
    <a title="Ceilidh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh"><img alt="Ceilidh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422140120p2/3229028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478171244?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceilidh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceilidh" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh">Ceilidh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478171244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5112620301380897737">WHAT THE HELL WAS THAT?! <br/><br/>Seriously, I was pretty horrified by the glorified violence in Divergent, but this manages to be close to psychotic. Am I supposed to sympathise with this man? He's nasty, completely incapable of making any sort of comment without immediately tacking on some sort of insult, has a very messed up moral core, and is incredibly whiny. <br/><br/>Here's my big issue with this and Divergent. They seem to think that violence is cool, and advocate its use pretty strongly. There's a horrifi</span>
  <span id="freeText5112620301380897737" style="display:none">WHAT THE HELL WAS THAT?! <br /><br />Seriously, I was pretty horrified by the glorified violence in Divergent, but this manages to be close to psychotic. Am I supposed to sympathise with this man? He's nasty, completely incapable of making any sort of comment without immediately tacking on some sort of insult, has a very messed up moral core, and is incredibly whiny. <br /><br />Here's my big issue with this and Divergent. They seem to think that violence is cool, and advocate its use pretty strongly. There's a horrific scene in the book involving a gun, which is the climax of the heroine discussing how secure and in charge she feels with a gun in her hand, that makes my blood curdle. Can we please stop it with this crap?<br /><br />This is a short and utterly pointless piece of writing that serves absolutely no purpose. It's bland, clunky, questionable in tone and intent, and completely fails as a character exercise. Tobias/Four started out as a jerk and remains one throughout Divergent. Here, nothing changes. In fact, he comes out of it being somewhat more psychotic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5112620301380897737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1196215776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196215776" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196215776?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-dystopian">fantasy-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196215776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17774371908160652400">This is a short story told from Four's POV of the knife-throwing scene from Divergent. It's a fast-paced short story that lets us know what Four was thinking: about Tris, Eric, and others in that moment. <br/><br/>Four is so swoon-worthy, it's hard to screw anything up if you are focusing on him. (Although, even though he's an ass, I did like the movie Eric, played by Jai Courtney. Dang, he's hot.)<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1720739195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720739195" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720739195?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=ya-dystopia">ya-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-2012">year-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720739195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14758086017082164967">I don't get why this story was even written. Basically, Veronica Roth retells a scene from the original <i>Divergent</i> novel by shifting the POV from Tris to Four, and she adds almost nothing to the character of Four what we didn't know yet except for minor details. Everything we learn in this story about his feelings was what could easily have been guessed after Divergent already, and the writing also wasn't particularly outstanding. Recommended for Divergent fans, but <i>only</i> for Divergent fans - this</span>
  <span id="freeText14758086017082164967" style="display:none">I don't get why this story was even written. Basically, Veronica Roth retells a scene from the original <i>Divergent</i> novel by shifting the POV from Tris to Four, and she adds almost nothing to the character of Four what we didn't know yet except for minor details. Everything we learn in this story about his feelings was what could easily have been guessed after Divergent already, and the writing also wasn't particularly outstanding. Recommended for Divergent fans, but <i>only</i> for Divergent fans - this short story won't make any sense if you read it before you read Divergent.<br /><br />I am disappointed, and by now even more convinced that I shouldn't continue with book #2 in the series. Alright, this is how marketing is done, this is how Veronica Roth and all the other people connected to the series probably earned quite some more money ... and yet I can't help asking myself, why was this needed? Why? </span>
  <a data-text-id="14758086017082164967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UB80yI1zcMOb0AYHlRQB8nTvMl7SWI4h2tx8Fr6mYafK8K9ny/u3I8j3/mSAs/7T4WPCWrgQdmiyFcDRKPiBfg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U5f6QYrc9OYHJNWoe4c+d36Mti8Lm0hsvbrLI/UUMrjJeGHuzFQzBlQDLctuIMFW6wBGK2HTsCXVc3fkY0rSYQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
